hairy
About the subscribers' problem and the video on TikTok with much more views than the one on YouTube, the reason is just the duration of videos. Usually, one person is subscribed to many channels on YouTube, but it's impossible to watch every video of every channel, because many channels have very long videos. So, you receive a notification that someone has put out a new video, and even if you don't know the length you assume that it could be long and you think: "I don't have time now,". On TikTok, you KNOW that the video is going to be VERY short and so you watch it and if you like it you share it with your friends knowing that a lot of them will watch it because it's soo short. This way, numbers grow up quickly. You really can't compare YouTube and TikTok views.
What if you play bass in the background of an entire video and add a bass cam? It would be an excuse to still make â€œbassâ€ videos that are long while still being a â€œbassâ€ video.

The reason Davie gets more views on TikTok rather than on YouTube is because on TikTok, when somebody is scrolling and comes to your video it counts as a view. But on YouTube you actually have to click on the video to count as a view. It is confusing but if you think about it, everytime Davie's video goes on the front page of YouTube it could count as a view on TikTok and not on YouTube

I think I know why your subscribers don't often see your videos in their feed - If you don't click the notification bell, it sorts recommended videos based on recent watch history.  If a given subscriber starts watching other types of videos a lot, it will get deprioritized severely.  There are channels I used to watch all the time that don't get placed very high on my feed anymore, because I watch mostly unrelated videos more frequently.  There have been channels, where I'll say to myself "I haven't seen a video from so and so for a while, I wonder if something happened?" and I'll go look  and find that they've been posting videos regularly, but YouTube just doesn't show them to me, because I've been watching different videos lately.  Subscriptions mean nothing compared to current viewing trends

"You have to put on your own mask before helping others."  This isn't the perfect fit for that well-known psychological health tip, but it's good enough.  Regardless of your intentions--to grow your YT channel, to reach and inspire people about bass, to be doing something you love for a living and have it show through--you've got to take care of yourself first, or everything else falls apart.  Good advice for every single person.  You'll get to 10M in a few months at most.  I'd say get it, get your diamond play button, make a thankful video (which I know is completely sincere), get the diamond play bass construction process going going, and then take a sabbatical.  Not a vacation; a sabbatical.  Sabbatical comes from "sabbath" which literally means "a time of rest."  Vacations are not restful.  Three months is a typical length for a sabbatical for people in stressful jobs.  Do whatever's necessary to rest, enjoy your time, think about things, NOT think about things, and just heal.  We'll be around.  It's stressful and lonely at the top.  We understand.  We'll still be here.

Davie, two weeks ago I decided to go back to BASS after 15 years - because of you.  I tried to become a bassist when there was no YT to help with the process. If you couldn't afford private lessons, you were basically on your own. I got stuck and ended up believing that I'm just not good enough to even try. Then 3 weeks ago one of your videos randomly popped up in my recommend and since then I binge watched your channel.  Your life story and love for Bass got me so excited that I really started to feel I could actually overcome one of my biggest insecurities and try again.  You are a huge inspiration to so many people, you bring joy and make the world better with your big SLAP energy. For that I will be forever grateful, thank you!!  And now please excuse me, I'm off to practice for another two hours ğŸ˜Š  PS. Please be good to yourself. Take all the time and care you need for your mental and physical health. YT burnout is a real thing... No one should feel such pressure.  It might be scary but remember that nothing lasts forever. These platforms change constantly, forcing their users to desperately change their tactics and themes in order to stay on the surface. In the end what is somebody's home for art and creativity is just a source of money for those who create and control it.  In some time there will be another big thing for creative people and YT will die out, as it already happend with MySpace, DeviantArt, Facebook... now Instagram is going down and YT probably will be next. It's a struggle. But there will come another invention that will give us a platform and opportunities to create what we love and to share it. We just cannot let it consume us.  Please remember that your mental health comes first!
